  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText5219068499465821401" style="display:none">New adventures lie ahead as Anne Shirley packs her bags, waves good-bye to childhood, and heads for Redmond College. With her old friend Prissy Grant waiting in the bustling city of Kingsport and her frivolous new friend Philippa Gordon at her side, Anne tucks her memories of rural Avonlea away and discovers life on her own terms, filled with surprises . . . including a marriage proposal from the worst fellow imaginable, the sale of her very first story, and a tragedy that teaches her a painful lesson. But tears turn to laughter when Anne and her friends move into an old cottage and an ornery black cat steals her heart. Little does Anne know that handsome Gilbert Blythe wants to win her heart, too. Suddenly Anne must decide whether she's ready for love.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2819853541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2825783844460861961">I know a lot of people are still waiting for their Hogwarts letter, and that’s fine and all, but I’m still over here waiting for my formal invitation to attend college with Anne and Gilbert and Philippa and the gang.<br/><br/>I’m sure it just got lost in the mail.<br/><br/>I adored <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1819372379' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anne of Green Gables</a> (in spite of the fact that I read it for the first time at 21 years old, on a whim, having no intention of reading it beforehand and, in fact, only having a copy at all because it was very pretty and I’m very book-sh</span>
  <span id="freeText2825783844460861961" style="display:none">I know a lot of people are still waiting for their Hogwarts letter, and that’s fine and all, but I’m still over here waiting for my formal invitation to attend college with Anne and Gilbert and Philippa and the gang.<br /><br />I’m sure it just got lost in the mail.<br /><br />I adored <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1819372379" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne of Green Gables</a> (in spite of the fact that I read it for the first time at 21 years old, on a whim, having no intention of reading it beforehand and, in fact, only having a copy at all because it was very pretty and I’m very book-shallow). Against all odds, I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2804587621" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne of Avonlea</a> just as much.<br /><br />And even more unlikely-ly, I loved Anne of the Island most of all. (So far.)<br /><br />The writing is beautiful. The settings are immersive. The storyline(s) are charming. And somehow all the characters are lovely, regardless of whether they’ve been there since the beginning or were just introduced two pages ago. I love all of them.<br /><br />So you understand my confusion at the fact that I have not yet been invited to Prince Edward Island, let alone accepted to Redmond College, LET ALONE inducted into Anne’s friend group.<br /><br />But like I said, I’m sure it’s just a matter of time.<br /><br />(I love this series way too much to consider the alternative.)<br /><br />Bottom line: GIVE ME THE NEXT ANNE BOOK!!! Please.<br /><br />------- <br /><br />i was late for work because i physically could not put this book down.<br /><br />review to come / 5 stars<br /><br />------- <br /><br />hello i would like to live inside these books and be best friends with anne and also be of the island thank you that is all</span>

<div id="review_2134676225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2134676225" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2134676225?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2134676225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11924355513967500554"><b>Now <i>this</i> is the college life I longed for</b><br/><br/>Anne Shirley is about to<b> do the unthinkable </b>- postpone marriage and attend off to Redmond College. She still plans to get married, but only after her education.<br/><br/>She's found a <b>darling house </b>to rent with Prissy Grant (from Avonlea) and Phillipa Gordon (from Redmond). <b> And now, her life will begin.</b><br/><br/>I loved the <b>feel</b> of this one - the hopeful wondering, the exciting change of scenery and the true friendships she finds. However. I do have a few issues with the wa</span>
  <span id="freeText11924355513967500554" style="display:none"><b>Now <i>this</i> is the college life I longed for</b><br /><br />Anne Shirley is about to<b> do the unthinkable </b>- postpone marriage and attend off to Redmond College. She still plans to get married, but only after her education.<br /><br />She's found a <b>darling house </b>to rent with Prissy Grant (from Avonlea) and Phillipa Gordon (from Redmond). <b> And now, her life will begin.</b><br /><br />I loved the <b>feel</b> of this one - the hopeful wondering, the exciting change of scenery and the true friendships she finds. However. I do have a few issues with the way this one is written. <br /><br />It almost feels like everything is solved too simply. All challenges are overcome with a bit of <b>plucky effort</b> and everything <b>always works out</b> just the way it needs to. Always. <br /><br />And honestly, the first two novels I didn't mind this...but by the third novel of such coincidences, I am starting to <b>grow a little tired </b>of the sheer <i>
  <b>perfection</b>
</i> of everything. <blockquote>
  <i>“It will come sometime. Some beautiful morning she will just wake up and find it is Tomorrow. Not Today but Tomorrow. And then things will happen ... wonderful things.” </i>
</blockquote> I still enjoy this series but there are <b>a few problems/inconsistencies</b> that are really throwing me off.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Dropping Diana Barry like a hot tamale</u>
</b><br /><br />Remember Diana Barry - <b>Anne's one, true bosom friend? </b><blockquote>
  <i>Kindred spirits alone do not change with the changing years.</i>
</blockquote> <b>Anne is such a liar. </b><br /><br />Diana Barry - who was so essential to the first books - is pushed aside now that Anne's in college and Diana's raising a family.<br /><br /> I understand that friends grow apart over time but if that was the case, there should be a paragraph or two explaining that. <br /><br />It's like...Diana was no longer useful to the plot so L. M. Montgomery just stopped writing about her. I mean, how hard would it be for Anne to write a few letters to Diana or for her to talk about missing her.<br /><br />I feel so betrayed on Diana's behalf.<b> So much for friendship.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Schrodinger Cat</u>
</b><br /><br />And I couldn't have been the only one completely <b>flabbergasted</b> by the cat story. <br /><br />Upon discovery of a semi-friendly tom cat, Anne, Prissy and Phillipa <b>
  <i>decide to kill it</i>
</b> with chloroform under a basket.<br /><br /> After leaving the cat under the deathtrap for a night, Anne lifts up the basket only to discover that <b>the cat survived.</b> She then adopts the cat and becomes best friends with the feline. <br /><br />You almost MURDERED the cat<b> - seriously, what the <i>hell </i>Anne?</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Revolving Plot</u>
</b><br /><br />There seems to be a<b> pattern to these books</b> - Anne meets new bosom friends, one grumpy/ornery one and one miserable one (due to bad luck with true love).<br /><br /><b>Anne befriends the grump,</b> tries (and ultimately fails) meddling in the miserable one's life...Then she learns <b>valuable life lessons</b> about not judging/meddling someone by their first impression. And everything ends happy.<br /><br />Repeat.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Concluding Thoughts</u>
</b><br /><br />Honestly, I'm more than a little disappointed by this one but not enough to stop the series. There were plenty of wonderful of moments and I really want to finish the series. Hopefully it picks up!<br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Read by Renée Raudman - and it was a rather pleasant audio to listen to.<br /><br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11924355513967500554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_7467915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7467915" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/122606-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454261971p2/122606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7467915?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/122606-chelsea">Chelsea</a>

  <span id="freeText9006347079571178358" style="display:none">Ah . . . more comfort food in the form of a book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472139414i/20157048.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After an eventful summer, changes are in store for Anne as she prepares to leave Avonlea for Redmond College.<br><br><b>Anne dressed in the cheerless gray dawn, for an early start was necessary to catch the boat train; she struggled against the tears that <i>would</i> well up in her eyes in spite of herself. She was leaving the home that was so dear to her, and something told her that she was leaving it forever, same as a holiday refuge. Things would never be the same again; coming back for vacations would not be living there. And oh, how dear and beloved everything was -- that little white porch room, sacred to the dreams of girlhood, the old Snow Queen at the window, the brook in the hollow, the Dryad's Bubble, the Haunted Wood, and Lover's Lane -- all the thousand and one dear spots where memories of the old years bided. Could she ever be really happy anywhere else?</b><br><br>But, there are new friends to meet and more challenges to conquer. Leaving home may bring heartache, but there is plenty of joy in store for our Anne.<br><br>This book covers four eventful years in Anne's life, including the hilarious circumstances surrounding the publication of her first short story, the death of an old schoolmate, and the marriage of another. Anne herself receives some mighty strange marriage proposals. This is my favorite:<br><br><b>"Yeh're a likely-looking girl and hev a right-smart way o' stepping," said Sam. "I don't want no lazy woman. Think it over. I won't change my mind yit awhile. Wall, I must be gitting. Gotter milk the cows."</b><br><br>This makes my husband's proposal of "You're sturdy enough for farm chores" seem almost romantic. (At least he didn't skedaddle off to feel up a bunch of cow's udders.)</span>

<div id="review_33443370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33443370" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50448-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1175789489p2/50448.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33443370?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/50448-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=2016reviews">2016reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer33443370&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33443370" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1774756332418881192">Montgomery, L.M. 1915. Anne of the Island.<br/><br/>"Harvest is ended and summer is gone," quoted Anne Shirley, gazing across the shorn fields dreamily.<br/><br/>I don't know if there are enough words to describe how I feel about Anne of the Island. It is one of the most magically, wonderful, giddy-making, purely-delightful, satisfying books I've ever read...and reread...and reread. Reading this book makes all the world seem right. (At least during the reading process.) It picks up shortly after where Anne of Avonl</span>
  <span id="freeText1774756332418881192" style="display:none">Montgomery, L.M. 1915. Anne of the Island.<br /><br />"Harvest is ended and summer is gone," quoted Anne Shirley, gazing across the shorn fields dreamily.<br /><br />I don't know if there are enough words to describe how I feel about Anne of the Island. It is one of the most magically, wonderful, giddy-making, purely-delightful, satisfying books I've ever read...and reread...and reread. Reading this book makes all the world seem right. (At least during the reading process.) It picks up shortly after where Anne of Avonlea leaves off. Anne Shirley and Gilbert Blythe are preparing to go off to Redmond college. (Along with Charlie Sloane and Priscilla Grant who you may or may not remember.) Diana Barry is engaged to Fred Wright. And there is a hint of love in the air.<br /><br />This is the story of Anne's college years; it spans four years. The books focus on her friendships with Priscilla Grant, Philippa Gordon, and Stella Maynard, her roommates. And of course the book focuses on her romantic-and-not-so-romantic dealings with men. Many men propose to Anne during the course of the book including Billy Andrews--who sends his sister in his place--and Sam Toliver with his bumbling, "Will yeh heve me?" (Charlie Sloane, Gilbert Blythe, and Royal Gardner are others.)<br /><br />There are many side stories in Anne of The Island. And while these little asides and tangents are not employed much in modern fiction, within the works of L.M. Montgomery, they are so thoroughly charming that they just work well. Really really well.<br /><br />I loved this one. Loved the romance. Loved the characters. Loved everything.<br /><br />Here's my favorite bit of the book:<br /><br />There is a book of Revelation in every one's life, as there is in the Bible. Anne read hers that bitter night, as she kept her agonized vigil through the hours of storm and darkness. She loved Gilbert—had always loved him! She knew that now. She knew that she could no more cast him out of her life without agony than she could have cut off her right hand and cast it from her. And the knowledge had come too late—too late even for the bitter solace of being with him at the last. If she had not been so blind—so foolish—she would have had the right to go to him now. But he would never know that she loved him—he would go away from this life thinking that she did not care. Oh, the black years of emptiness stretching before her! She could not live through them—she could not! She cowered down by her window and wished, for the first time in her gay young life, that she could die, too. If Gilbert went away from her, without one word or sign or message, she could not live. Nothing was of any value without him. She belonged to him and he to her. In her hour of supreme agony she had no doubt of that. He did not love Christine Stuart—never had loved Christine Stuart. Oh, what a fool she had been not to realize what the bond was that had held her to Gilbert—to think that the flattered fancy she had felt for Roy Gardner had been love. And now she must pay for her folly as for a crime. (237)<br /><br />© Becky Laney of Becky's Book Reviews</span>
  <a data-text-id="1774756332418881192" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1871617733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9772966630866661970">Holy crap, do you guys know what this is?! It’s a New Adult book that was written ONE HUNDRED YEARS AGO! (Seriously, that’s what this is!) I had no idea this sub-genre existed back then, lol! <br/><br/>College? Check. Relationship drama and angst? Check. Sassy, funny girlfriend? Check. Handsome, cocky love interest? Che— Wait, NO. No, no, nope! Move over all you hot, arrogant assholes, cuz Gilbert Blythe blows ALL of you out of the fricken water!<br/><br/>I totally loved this. LOVED. THIS.<br/><br/>Love love love love love :</span>
  <span id="freeText9772966630866661970" style="display:none">Holy crap, do you guys know what this is?! It’s a New Adult book that was written ONE HUNDRED YEARS AGO! (Seriously, that’s what this is!) I had no idea this sub-genre existed back then, lol! <br /><br />College? Check. Relationship drama and angst? Check. Sassy, funny girlfriend? Check. Handsome, cocky love interest? Che— Wait, NO. No, no, nope! Move over all you hot, arrogant assholes, cuz Gilbert Blythe blows ALL of you out of the fricken water!<br /><br />I totally loved this. LOVED. THIS.<br /><br />Love love love love love :)<br /><br />There were a lot of different things to love in the first book (and I loved it all), but I’ll admit that the thing that REALLY hooked me in was the cute rivalry between Anne and Gilbert. Oh, those two. . .<br /><br />Omg, the angst! I had no idea! I didn’t know this book was gonna make me feel like this. All frustrated and hopeful and swoony and annoyed. <br /><br />(I’m guessing I’m the only person on the planet who hasn’t ever read/seen this series before, but I’ll just spoiler tag anyway :P)<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br /><br />My heart thumped like crazy at so many parts! Like here:<br /><br /><b><i>“This is what I would once have called an epoch in my life,” said Anne, as she took Roy’s violets out of their box and gazed at them thoughtfully. She meant to carry them, of course, but her eyes wandered to another box on her table. It was filled with lilies-of-the-valley, as fresh and fragrant as those which bloomed in the Green Gables yard when June came to Avonlea. Gilbert Blythe’s card lay beside it.</i></b><br /><br />(me: OH MY GOOOOODDDDD HE SENT HER FLOWERS EEEEEEK!!!!!)<br /><br /><br /><b><i>. . .the flash in Gilbert’s eyes when he saw her lilies. . .</i></b><br /><br />(me: OMG he sees that she chose HIS flowers to wear instead of Roy's COME ON YOU GUYS I MEAN SERIOUSLY JUST COME <i>ON!!!!!!</i>)<br /><br /><br /><b><i>“I have a dream,” he said slowly. “I persist in dreaming it, although it has often seemed to me that it could never come true.”</i></b><br /><br />(me: holy shit it’s really happening. IT’S REALLY HAPPENING!!!)<br /><br /><br /><br /><b><i>“There was nobody else - there never could be anybody else for me but you. I’ve loved you ever since that day you broke your slate over my head in school.”</i></b><br /><br />Me: *sighs happily* No words. Completely satisfied.<br /><br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9772966630866661970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3076744429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11755962101253844585">Interesting fact I learned recently - L.M. Montgomery studied at my school, Dalhousie University, in the late 1800's. I guess Dal here has had some pretty interesting people study on its campus. Kind of eerie (not in a bad way) to think of someone studying here over a hundred years ago like that.<br/><br/><i>Anne of the Island</i> is one of several in the Anne of Green Gables series which I hadn't yet read, and it's a really great one. Anne is leaving for Redmond College in Nova Scotia, something which takes her</span>
  <span id="freeText11755962101253844585" style="display:none">Interesting fact I learned recently - L.M. Montgomery studied at my school, Dalhousie University, in the late 1800's. I guess Dal here has had some pretty interesting people study on its campus. Kind of eerie (not in a bad way) to think of someone studying here over a hundred years ago like that.<br /><br /><i>Anne of the Island</i> is one of several in the Anne of Green Gables series which I hadn't yet read, and it's a really great one. Anne is leaving for Redmond College in Nova Scotia, something which takes her on a new adventure away from teaching where she finds a whole new lifestyle. While initially she stays in a boarding house, she and her friends move into a cottage. However, this book isn't only about Anne's collage life. The characters from the previous novels in Avonlea are all still entwined in their original stories, and Anne finds herself questioning her friendship/love for Gilbert as she holds onto other ideals.<br /><br />Montgomery's writing really portrays Nova Scotia very well scenically and in terms of the people living here - yeah, it might be over a century ahead now, but some things are still exactly as described in this book. <i>Anne of the Island</i> also avoids a saccharine fairytale love story by exploring the complications and joys life can present in a realistic, honest way that still ends up being uplifting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11755962101253844585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10360043477352479218">Eeeeeeeeeeeeeee!!!! :D :D :D :D<br/><br/>I loved this book SOOOOO much!! Probably as much as the first book, if not maybe even a little bit more! :)) It was really hard at first to determine which one I liked better, but I think I like <i>Anne of the Island</i> more since she just starts college and all ^_^ I felt like I could relate to her and the things she went through more in this book. There were so many little, tiny things that I enjoyed about this book, but the main thing I loved…....(I think you can gues</span>
  <span id="freeText10360043477352479218" style="display:none">Eeeeeeeeeeeeeee!!!! :D :D :D :D<br><br>I loved this book SOOOOO much!! Probably as much as the first book, if not maybe even a little bit more! :)) It was really hard at first to determine which one I liked better, but I think I like <i>Anne of the Island</i> more since she just starts college and all ^_^ I felt like I could relate to her and the things she went through more in this book. There were so many little, tiny things that I enjoyed about this book, but the main thing I loved…....(I think you can guess what that is by now XD lol)..….it’s Anne &amp; Gilbert &lt;3 &lt;3 They will forever be my favorite fictional couple! ^_^ I really liked that they were friends/enemies ;) hehe since they were kids before they even thought about starting a relationship. I felt like Anne was being a little stupid at times about what she expected in a relationship, but I’m glad she finally figured out who was best for her in the end ;)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411671821ra/11263676.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I also really enjoyed getting to see Anne and her friends go to college and pick out a home to live in. When they picked their house, Patty’s Place, there was this cat that followed Anne home and she and her roommates didn’t want it living with them, so they did this really sad—but also kind of funny :p—thing to it…Anne’s roommate, Philippa or Phil, tried to chloroform it to kill it and that scene was a little cruel and hilarious at the same time XD *cowers in shame* hehe I seriously didn’t mean to laugh at that scene, but I couldn’t help it haha…I’m glad that it didn’t end up dying though because I would have felt terrible if it did :p<br><br>I’ve mentioned this before, but I just really adore the characters in this series!! ^_^ They all seem like old friends now or ‘chums’, as they call it in the book, and I enjoy just reading about their day-to-day lives...By now, I think everyone on Goodreads knows how much I love the Anne of Green Gables series hehe so of course, I think all of you should go and pick these books up ;) <br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer737612915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8326370829674037280">After this book the series has lost its charm, I don't think I'll read any of the other books. This wasn't exactly a bad book... just kind of tedious. It takes place over 3 years and goes between Anne being at college and at Green Gables. <br/><br/>The best part: Anne and Gilbert finally get together!<br/><br/>The good part: It's fun to see Anne and her friends making a home out of Patty's place, even if her new friend Phil is extremely annoying.<br/><br/>The bad part: Davy is still disturbing to read about. He cries because</span>
  <span id="freeText8326370829674037280" style="display:none">After this book the series has lost its charm, I don't think I'll read any of the other books. This wasn't exactly a bad book... just kind of tedious. It takes place over 3 years and goes between Anne being at college and at Green Gables. <br /><br />The best part: Anne and Gilbert finally get together!<br /><br />The good part: It's fun to see Anne and her friends making a home out of Patty's place, even if her new friend Phil is extremely annoying.<br /><br />The bad part: Davy is still disturbing to read about. He cries because he missed the "fun" of seeing Mrs. Lynde fall down the cellar stairs and hurt herself. Anne is proposed to 6 times. She turns down pretty much every one of them, it gets a little silly. <br /><br />The worst part: The author is constantly inserting her views on god and politics into the story.<br /><br />The horrifying part: Anne and her friends find a stray cat and they decide to kill it by putting it into a box with chloroform. WTF. Even worse, Mr. Harrison decides he doesn't want his dog anymore so he hangs it. After it survives and tries to hide in the barn, he hangs it again. WTF. I know things were different back then but WTF!!! It's horrifying how calm they all are about murdering animals when they get so offended by statements like "God knows." </span>
  <a data-text-id="8326370829674037280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2650428947" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2650428947" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2650428947?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=favourites-read">favourites-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=college-story">college-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=l-m-montgomery">l-m-montgomery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2650428947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5525282684703069854">I absolutely do love love love Lucy Maud Montgomery's <i>Anne of Green Gables</i> series, and indeed, especially the third book, in particular her <u>Anne of the Island</u> is and always will be a total favourite, and yes, a very special and personal favourite that I have in fact and actually read more than ANY of the other series books, including the first novel, including <u>Anne of Green Gables</u> (with my conservative guesstimate being that my reading amount for <u>Anne of Green Gables</u> is probably around ten times</span>
  <span id="freeText5525282684703069854" style="display:none">I absolutely do love love love Lucy Maud Montgomery's <i>Anne of Green Gables</i> series, and indeed, especially the third book, in particular her <u>Anne of the Island</u> is and always will be a total favourite, and yes, a very special and personal favourite that I have in fact and actually read more than ANY of the other series books, including the first novel, including <u>Anne of Green Gables</u> (with my conservative guesstimate being that my reading amount for <u>Anne of Green Gables</u> is probably around ten times but that I have read, laughed and cried over <u>Anne of the Island</u> probably twenty times and perhaps even considerably more than that). <br /><br />Honestly and truth be told, I definitely and certainly massively both adore and appreciate absolutely everything about <u>Anne of the Island</u>. Anne Shirley finally going to Redmond College to get her BA, her rather humorous but also a bit frustrating travails trying to learn how to write proper and not too exaggerated, too overwrought fiction, her on and off again romantic entanglements with Gilbert Blythe and yes, even poor Ruby Gillis' death from consumption (although part of me has always chafed that L.M. Montgomery could not have let Ruby live), all of these (and of course many many more) episodes and anecdotes, they always make me feel comforted, and like a hot cup of tea, <u>Anne of the Island</u> is to and for me a panacea to and for both my and the world's ills and woes. But still and nevertheless, even though totally like a blanket of loveliness and softly positive wonder, <u>Anne of the Island</u> also portrays sadness (and even tragedy) at times, albeit always in a manner that is easily digestible and tolerable, acceptable, perhaps even necessary and required, and with the glowing and very much appreciated fact that L.M. Montgomery makes most of her characters, makes Anne, Stella, Priscilla, Philippa, Diana etc. appear, act as realistically conceptualised individuals with both positive and negative characteristics, and also has them make their share of mistakes (such as for example how Anne Shirley at times a bit callously approaches and deals with Gilbert Blythe, and her acceptance and then rather harsh refusal of Roy Gardiner before finally managing to realise that Gilbert truly is the one for her) being the absolute icing on the cake for me (even though I do sometimes tend to find that episode of Gilbert being ill with typhoid before Anne realises how much she loves him just a bit too much). For what makes the <i>Anne of Green Gables</i> series as a whole and what in my opinion makes especially <u>Anne of the Island</u> so delightfully wonderful and readable, relatable, is how deeply developed and nuanced Montgomery's characters for the most part are, how none or at least how the vast majority of them are never one-sided, are both lovable and sometimes indeed most annoyingly infuriating (that the characters who inhabit the pages of <u>Anne of the Island</u> have been rendered by Montgomery as basically real and breathing, living human beings, individuals whom one can both like/love but also occasionally not stand, a wonderfully both imaginative and realistic reading experience that is like a breath of fresh air and a total personally enchanting and endearing comfort whenever I decide to reread).</span>
  <a data-text-id="5525282684703069854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer127525691925379298">Anne is a little older and goes to school at Redmont with her friend, Prissy. Along the way they meet Phillippa Gordon (who may be my favorite character so far in the series, I mean besides Anne of course!). Phil, Prissy, and Anne find a house to let -- quaint and practically perfect. The house is called Patty's Place and they all soon move in. They find themselves with three cats- a fireplace, and imagination which makes for a lovely setting. Anne is trying to figure out what love is and how sh</span>
  <span id="freeText127525691925379298" style="display:none">Anne is a little older and goes to school at Redmont with her friend, Prissy. Along the way they meet Phillippa Gordon (who may be my favorite character so far in the series, I mean besides Anne of course!). Phil, Prissy, and Anne find a house to let -- quaint and practically perfect. The house is called Patty's Place and they all soon move in. They find themselves with three cats- a fireplace, and imagination which makes for a lovely setting. Anne is trying to figure out what love is and how she feels about it, she gets proposed to multiple times (a few times elicited chuckles from me) and finally meets Roy Gardner- a wealthy man that meets Anne under an umbrella after "rescuing" her from the sudden rainstorm. (sigh)<br /><br />I really enjoyed Anne at this age, even still her stubborness got in her own way in regards to Gilbert. I almost got to a point where I would never forgive her, but luckily it all worked out in the end. THis book was more mature and as a byproduct had sadder events that tug at my heartstrings<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ (Ruby Gillis) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Looking forward to the next book in Anne's story.</span>

Every time you see that person, it grows and grows until eventually something needs to be done about it either way. <div id="review_2377737389" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2377737389" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2377737389?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=classics-i-ve-read">classics-i-ve-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2377737389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4300989248216208136">This is going to be short and sweet. As with the previous two books, I thoroughly enjoyed this installment in the story of Anne Shirley’s life. Here, we see Anne attending college and fighting against the assumptions of others regarding her love life. She makes new friends and a new home and watches as old friends and Green Gables begin to change. It’s hard growing up and seeing that life doesn’t stay the same, and Anne struggles with this. She also struggles with her love life. There’s a bit of</span>
  <span id="freeText4300989248216208136" style="display:none">This is going to be short and sweet. As with the previous two books, I thoroughly enjoyed this installment in the story of Anne Shirley’s life. Here, we see Anne attending college and fighting against the assumptions of others regarding her love life. She makes new friends and a new home and watches as old friends and Green Gables begin to change. It’s hard growing up and seeing that life doesn’t stay the same, and Anne struggles with this. She also struggles with her love life. There’s a bit of a love triangle here, which I always hate, and Anne is downright silly and ignorant in her desire to not love a particular someone, but everything works out right in the end. As with all of these books, there’s lots of humor, and a multitude of profound statements. I love the mix of depth and levity Montgomery is able to produce with such deftness. Although I didn’t enjoy this book quite as much as the two before it, it’s still a lovely story. I’ve never made it beyond this book in the eight-book series, so I’m excited to see what happens next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4300989248216208136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_257898011" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257898011" />
    <a title="kris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2125614-kris"><img alt="kris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325962640p2/2125614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257898011?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kris" href="/user/show/2125614-kris">kris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257898011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6507840971095090905">Anne Shirley goes to Redmond, makes friends, discovers boys are A Thing, and returns to Green Gables and Avonlea which she is startled to realize no longer feel quite like home. <br/><br/>Every time I try to approach these books logically to provide a thorough critique and commentary on them, my soul cries out and I'm left clutching fistfuls of tears shouting about my childhood. There's something so intrinsically linked to who I was when I first read them that I can't separate myself from them. <br/><br/>It's just </span>
  <span id="freeText6507840971095090905" style="display:none">Anne Shirley goes to Redmond, makes friends, discovers boys are A Thing, and returns to Green Gables and Avonlea which she is startled to realize no longer feel quite like home. <br /><br />Every time I try to approach these books logically to provide a thorough critique and commentary on them, my soul cries out and I'm left clutching fistfuls of tears shouting about my childhood. There's something so intrinsically linked to who I was when I first read them that I can't separate myself from them. <br /><br />It's just so cozy and heartening reading about the girls settling into Patty's Place and making lives for themselves, even as many of the details get swept to the side in the hurry of cramming four years into one volume. I wanted more of those quiet evenings studying, or the rambunctious evenings when they were home to friends, or the festive nights when they went out to parties and dances. <br /><br />I was also a bit thrown by some of the casual violence this time around: chloroforming Rusty; hanging the dog; Mrs. Lynde falling down the cellar steps; Ruby's death; Mrs. Josephine Barry's death—I feel like these things were stepped over or rushed over without too much weight. <br /><br />ALSO, I put from my mind the fact that Anne is "not overly fond" of cats. I mean, really. <br /><br />In addition, I found myself the smallest bit frustrated with how conveniently perfect everything works out for Anne: Patty and Maria choosing to be gone for 3 years exactly, returning in May after graduation; Mrs. Barry's death giving Anne enough money to stay on at Redmond; etc. It's a wonderful story, but it does make for a kind of easy, eye-rolling sensation of <i>of course it'll all be all right; how could it not?</i> that went down like syrup. <br /><br />After wanting more about Diana settling into Avonlea, now I'm hungry for a glimpse into Gilbert Blythe's days at college: working at a newspaper, deciding to become a doctor, seeing Anne out and about and feeling heartbroken, befriending Christine and getting along with her without any other expectations. <br /><br />BUT STILL: "I have a dream," he said slowly. "I persist in dreaming it, although it has often seemed to me that it could never come true. I dream of a home with a hearth-fire in it, a cat and dog, the foot-steps of friends—and YOU!"<br /><br />PS: Not enough kissing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6507840971095090905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer69636183" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17130682827004771691">When I get to heaven, I want to meet Lucy Maud Montgomery! What insight the woman had, and what depth. I loved the first book for its tenderness and vitality, the second for its insight and humor. This book had all of those things, but added something more--tremendous depth. I believe the theme of this book is maturity, and the old characters as well as some new ones gain and display this quality without making the book at all dry or humorless--it is quite the opposite. Of course, there are othe</span>
  <span id="freeText17130682827004771691" style="display:none">When I get to heaven, I want to meet Lucy Maud Montgomery! What insight the woman had, and what depth. I loved the first book for its tenderness and vitality, the second for its insight and humor. This book had all of those things, but added something more--tremendous depth. I believe the theme of this book is maturity, and the old characters as well as some new ones gain and display this quality without making the book at all dry or humorless--it is quite the opposite. Of course, there are other themes as well, not the least of which is love. But I wouldn't spoil the book for you--just read it! (P.S. This book helped me to realize that the movie "Anne of Green Gables: The Sequel," which I have loved all my life, must now be sold. I will never be able to enjoy it the same way again, knowing what the story was meant to be!) </span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText17380262760427209822" style="display:none">I loved going away to college with Anne. Her life there with her friends at Patty's Place just exudes charm and cozy-feelings. Of course, I was thrilled with the happily-ever-after, while completely relating to Anne's nostalgia about days gone by. I think Anne, and myself, needed the reminder that even when it's sad to leave the former things behind, there are always good things to come. Anne is such an indescribably charismatic character, one that is sincere and lovely to be around. The secondary characters are always so fun - my favorites in this one are Phillipa and Aunt Jimsie - they just made me smile. I'm so eager to read the next installment in the series.</span>

<div id="review_99909759" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99909759" />
    <a title="Anita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2135974-anita"><img alt="Anita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351512087p2/2135974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99909759?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anita" href="/user/show/2135974-anita">Anita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2135974-anita?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2135974-anita?shelf=i-like-you-fiction">i-like-you-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2135974-anita?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2135974-anita?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99909759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14234468653279040617">It's a sad reminder how times change when you approach the bookstore with a gleam in your eye of rediscovering a childhood favorite only to find that they no longer carry it. That was my recent experience where instead of finding Laura Ingalls Wilder and L.M. Montgomery I found vampires, sorcery, and scantily clad teenagers glaring at me from overly bright and shiny bookcovers.<br/>I will not claim that the Anne series is monumental fiction but it was too me. I wonder if youth today are getting in th</span>
  <span id="freeText14234468653279040617" style="display:none">It's a sad reminder how times change when you approach the bookstore with a gleam in your eye of rediscovering a childhood favorite only to find that they no longer carry it. That was my recent experience where instead of finding Laura Ingalls Wilder and L.M. Montgomery I found vampires, sorcery, and scantily clad teenagers glaring at me from overly bright and shiny bookcovers.<br />I will not claim that the Anne series is monumental fiction but it was too me. I wonder if youth today are getting in their own reading what I so very much treasured in the books of my childhood. In twenty years will they fondly remember those manga (?) books or recall the great vampire trend? Will they be the ones saying how times have changed? Probably.<br />I love Anne. She is simple and complex she is delightful and innocent. I would love to be just like her minus the red hair. She lives in beautiful environments and has an amazing time wherever she goes.<br />I guess there will always be crud sold as literature which is what I called all those books taking over the precious spots my Anne should have been in, but wasn't it I who loved R.L. Stines Fear Street series twenty years ago too? And isn't it I who have wonderful memories of reading that crud as a kid? I guess so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14234468653279040617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2929349704" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2929349704" />
    <a title="m a r y l i z" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56772107-m-a-r-y-l-i-z"><img alt="m a r y l i z" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591561393p2/56772107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2929349704?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="m a r y l i z" class="user" itemprop="url" name="m a r y l i z" href="/user/show/56772107-m-a-r-y-l-i-z">m a r y l i z</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442490055" href="/book/show/18689753-anne-of-the-island">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2929349704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17281083673674996505"><b>"I don't want sunbursts and marble halls. I just want <i>you.</i>"</b><br/><br/>Just going to say right up front: <b>absolutely none of the books in this series can come close to the beauty of the first Anne book.</b> It's a slice of magical, golden childhood and I will defend that book with my life. :')<br/><br/>Secondly: I've literally been shipping Anne & Gilbert since before I even knew shipping was a thing. And they fINALLY have their Moment!!! <br/> <br/><i>"There was nobody else--there never could be anybody else for me but you. I've love</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17281083673674996505" style="display:none"><b>"I don't want sunbursts and marble halls. I just want <i>you.</i>"</b><br /><br />Just going to say right up front: <b>absolutely none of the books in this series can come close to the beauty of the first Anne book.</b> It's a slice of magical, golden childhood and I will defend that book with my life. :')<br /><br />Secondly: I've literally been shipping Anne &amp; Gilbert since before I even knew shipping was a thing. And they fINALLY have their Moment!!! <br /> <br /><i>"There was nobody else--there never could be anybody else for me but you. I've loved you ever since that day you broke your slate over my head in school."</i><br /><br />Oh look, that's me dissolved in a puddle of happy feels. <br /><br /><b>Other things I liked:</b><br /><br />- The writing style is soft &amp; unassumingly lush. It's such a comforting &amp; homey thing to get lost in.<br /><br /><i>March came in that winter like the meekest and mildest of lambs, bringing days that were crisp and golden and tingling, each followed by a frosty pink twilight which gradually lost itself in an elfland of moonshine.</i><br /><br />- Avonlea is like a second home to me now.<br /><br />- Phil is a <i>riot</i> and she injected so much life into this story.<br /><br />- All the college/change-related stuff was super relevant to my life right now. I know exactly how Anne feels watching all her old friends get in relationships and feeling left out. It's so hard to articulate, but this has been happening to me a lot &amp; I relate to Anne's dread of changing relationships. You desperately want things to remain the same, familiar way they always did. But people (and relationships) change . . . and that's a hard thing to accept. <br /><br />- Patty's Place is the coziest little home imaginable. I want that to be my new dorm room, please and thank you.<br /><br />- Marilla getting all sentimental and nearly making me <i>C R Y</i>. (Also, I still miss Matthew, terribly. &lt;3)<br /><br />- I know I already mentioned this, but <i>Anne and Gilbert.</i> They were probably my first OTP, and they finallyyyyyyyyyy get together by the end of this book. I wanted to shake some sense into Anne because it took her the entirety of college to figure out she liked him. *facepalm*<br /><br />- I just feel so light and happy reading L.M. Montgomery's books. I'm sure this doesn't need any explanation.<br /><br /><b>Things I didn't like:</b><br /><br />- Not enough of all the "classic" Avonlea characters (Marilla, Diana, Gilbert, etc.). They're like family to me, and I missed them. I like the new "school chums" that Anne makes, but I almost feel like Anne's friendship with Diana is forgotten. :/ <br /><br />- OKAY. So. Rant time. This is the major reason I docked off an extra star. I'm a huge animal lover, so the one chapter where they try to freaking chloroform a cat they couldn't take care of??? <b>I. Was. So. Upset.</b> I don't care that it's a different time period. I don't even care that they were "trying to not cause the cat pain." THAT'S NO EXCUSE.<br /><br />I know people are probably rolling their eyes right now. Like, "Seriously, Mary, it's supposed to be <i>funny.</i> Stop making such a big deal out of nothing."<br /><br />Well, I'm sorry, but I fail to see any humor in the fact that they actually tried to kill an animal they couldn't take care of. That's never okay, and it made me so furious &amp; disturbed. It seemed so out of character for Anne, and worse, it was never portrayed in a negative way. <br /><br />If you can't keep an animal . . . find someone who will be able to. I don't know how anyone can justify this.<br /><br />*deep breath* I'm sorry, but despite how much I love these characters, that chapter was sickening. <br /><br />- It could get a little boring at times &amp; it lacked the magic of the first book. But that's mostly just because I was pining for all of Anne's hilarious antics and adventures with the classic Avonlea gang. <br /><br />Overall? This was a delightful, transportive experience. L.M. Montgomery never fails to make my heart thrill with nostalgia and happiness. This may not be the standard of golden perfection that <i>Anne of Green Gables</i> is, but it was a much-needed book for this period of my life. <br /><br /><b>3.5 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17281083673674996505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kYTQflVmcQa8BR2mgyh65RoJyd9k0i7fsLwmKAsiOCirorms7ji4bhsuqcd03XA6zFYuF6pfoLjrwmCZxmHKsg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YyYruVIoKh68ztUZbVWMAenCl6ef5Q4gwIMJq5d2aXJZAEJr6XbjdhvlYXiaoIbeP51wb1FogEeb/U8aWjWb6A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

The story of the spunky red-haired orphan from Prince Edward Island is known to millions, and copies of the eight titles in the series have never gone out of print. \n\nBut when readers first meet Anne, she is eleven and has just been sent from an orphanage to meet her new family. No one ever learned the events of Anne\'s life before she arrived at Green Gables. \n\nUntil now. \n\nFor the millions of readers who devoured the Green Gables series, Before Green Gables is an <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer375538187555201025"><b>Lucy Maud Montgomery</b> was a Canadian author, best known for a series of novels beginning with Anne of Green Gables, published in 1908.<br/><br/>The author of the famous Canadian novel Anne of Green Gables, Lucy Maud Montgomery, was born at Clifton, Prince Edward Island, Nov. 30, 1874. She came to live at Leaskdale, north of Uxbridge Ontario, in 1911 after her wedding with Rev. Ewen Macdonald on July 11, 1911</span>
  <span id="freeText375538187555201025" style="display:none"><b>Lucy Maud Montgomery</b> was a Canadian author, best known for a series of novels beginning with Anne of Green Gables, published in 1908.<br /><br />The author of the famous Canadian novel Anne of Green Gables, Lucy Maud Montgomery, was born at Clifton, Prince Edward Island, Nov. 30, 1874. She came to live at Leaskdale, north of Uxbridge Ontario, in 1911 after her wedding with Rev. Ewen Macdonald on July 11, 1911 in Prince Edward Island. Her three children were born at Leaskdale, and she wrote close to a dozen books while she was living in the Leaskdale Manse before the Macdonald family moved to Norval, Ontario in 1926. <br /><br />Maud died in Toronto April 24, 1942 and was buried at Cavendish, Prince Edward Island.<br /><br />For more information, please see <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucy_Maud_Montgomery">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucy_Mau...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="375538187555201025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

Rilla, almost fifteen, can\'t think any further ahead than going to her very first dance at the Four Winds lighthouse and getting her first kiss from handsome Kenneth Ford. But undreamed-of challenges await the irrepressible Rilla when the world of Ingleside is endangered by a far-off war. Montgomery to be the ninth volume in her bestselling series featuring her beloved heroine Anne – and delivered to he<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText13320229884731311098\" style=\"display:none\">The Blythes Are Quoted is the last work of fiction by the internationally celebrated author of Anne of Green Gables. Intended by L.M. Montgomery to be the ninth volume in her bestselling series featuring her beloved heroine Anne – and delivered to her publisher on the very day she died – it has never before been published in its entirety. This rediscovered volume marks the final word of a writer whose work continues to fascinate readers all over the world.\n\nAdultery, illegitimacy, revenge, murder, and death – these are not the first terms we associate with L.M. Montgomery. But in The Blythes Are Quoted, completed at the end of her life,the author brings topics such as these to the fore.\n\nIntended by Montgomery to be the ninth volume in her bestselling series featuring Anne Shirley Blythe, The Blythes Are Quoted takes Anne and her family a full two decades beyond anything else she published about them, and some of its subject matter is darker than we might expect.\n\nDivided into two sections, one set before and one after the Great War of 1914–1918, it contains fifteen short stories set in and around the Blythes’ Prince Edward Island community of Glen St. Mary. Binding these stories are sketches featuring Anne and Gilbert Blythe discussing poems by Anne and their middle son, Walter, who dies as a soldier in the war. By blending together poetry, prose, and dialogue in this way, Montgomery was at the end of her career experimenting with storytelling methods in an entirely new manner.\n\nThis publication of Montgomery\'s rediscovered original work – previously published only in severely abridged form as The Road to Yesterday – invites readers to return to her earlier books with a renewed appreciation and
